Hoping the Soviets Can Abandon Their Prejudices and Cooperate for World Peace, Truman Points Out Stalin's Hidden Concerns 40

[Our Newspaper Report] New York, 12th Broadcast: President Truman gave a speech at the University of California today, discussing Soviet-U.S. relations. The tone was more severe than ever before. It is said that "the Soviet Union's refusal to cooperate for world peace is extremely disappointing, but there is still hope that the Soviet side will abandon its prejudices and participate in sincere negotiations on peace." President Truman cited the following facts of Soviet refusal to cooperate: (1) Refusal to participate in the European Recovery Program; (2) Unreasonable use of the veto power in the United Nations; (3) Indirect aggression against Eastern European countries and pressure on Middle Eastern countries; (4) Using the Communist Party to interfere in the internal affairs of other countries. Truman continued that what the Soviet Union is resisting is not only the United States but the whole world. The United States has no aggressive ambitions towards the Soviet Union or any other country. If countries around the world want to restore security, they must end the Soviet Union's aggressive behavior. In this regard, Truman listed the Soviet Union's actions in Greece and Korea as evidence.

[Central News Agency Reporter Lu Qixin Following the U.S. President's Entourage, Eugene, Oregon True Telegram] President Truman claimed here tonight that he admired his [old friend] Stalin, and that he got along well with Mr. Stalin during the Potsdam Conference. He said that the Soviet leader was a noble man. Truman made the above remarks to a large audience gathered here on his special train to San Francisco. While reiterating the United States' desire for world peace, Truman said that when he went to the Potsdam Conference, he had the greatest goodwill towards the Soviet Union and had reached some special agreements with Stalin. He said that although he expressed personal feelings of friendship towards Stalin, Mr. Stalin was ultimately a prisoner of the Politburo and could not act according to his own will. Truman also said that Stalin would abide by the agreements he signed whenever possible, but people in the Soviet government stated unequivocally that Stalin could not abide by the agreements. President Truman expressed his belief that the United States and the Soviet Union will one day realize their mutual interests, which lie in the peace and happiness of the whole world.

Bidault Defends Six-Nation Agreement; Fate of French Cabinet Hinges On It; Prime Minister Schuman Plans to Request Vote of Confidence from Parliament 41

[Reuters Paris, 11th] The National Assembly today listened to Foreign Minister Bidault's defense of the London six-nation conference resolution on West Germany for two hours in a quiet atmosphere, with only members of the People's Republican Party and a few moderate members occasionally applauding and cheering. The outcome of this debate may determine the fate of the Schuman cabinet. The debate will continue on the 12th, and the London conference resolution will be put to a vote next Tuesday. It is rumored that Foreign Minister Bidault will resign after the vote, but this claim has not been confirmed.

Bidault's speech emphasized that the resolutions of the London six-nation conference did not neglect security guarantees for Europe and France. On the contrary, it guarantees that Germany will not be able to use the Ruhr to control and influence the economies of its neighbors. In addition, based on this agreement, France has for the first time obtained the guarantee from the United States that US troops will continue to be stationed in important areas of Germany, even after the end of the general occupation. Bidault also stated that he did not feel any special interest in the suggestion of convening a German constitutional assembly before September 1. The French government has only one condition: that the regime established in Germany should not allow the Soviet Union to unilaterally retain excessive or controlling power. Germany must not become a tool of any allied country. Apart from this, the Soviet Union can participate in the institutions proposed to be established in Germany at any time, and we hope to reach an agreement with the Soviet Union as quickly as possible. Bidault then earnestly appealed to the parliament to approve this six-nation agreement, saying: "I sincerely hope that you will not allow France to fall into isolation. I am not a person who is easily repentant. You can believe that I never express unreasonable approval or unreasonable excuses. The French government is not unaware of the danger of Germany being divided into two, but this is a state for which France cannot be held responsible. The French government also understands the situation in Berlin and does not underestimate the danger there. The French government will repeatedly state that its ultimate goal is still to reach an agreement with the allied countries. The French government hopes that the Soviet government will soon join with other allied countries to seek a solution to the German peace treaty issue. What the French government is facing today is a choice between cooperating with allied countries or remaining isolated. The French government believes that the resolutions of the London Conference are acceptable. Although the resolutions are not perfect, they must first be approved to make them formally established before they can be improved." It is rumored that Prime Minister Schuman plans to make the vote on the London conference resolution on Tuesday a vote of confidence for the government. Political figures believe that this move can allow the government to obtain a relatively majority of support.

Romanian Industry and Mining All Nationalized 42

[United Press Budapest, 11th] Romania, in a lightning-like action, has nationalized almost all of its industry, mining, oil wells, and natural resources. This nationalization bill, which was adopted in a secret cabinet meeting today, was sent to parliament at 11:30 a.m. The parliament passed it unanimously after three hours of debate. The bill declares that from today, all oil fields, 720 industrial companies including factories, mines, oil fields, railways, and radio and telephones, are the property of the state. The list of state-owned enterprises also includes foreign-invested oil companies, most of which are British and American investors. The bill allows the owners of the expropriated properties to be compensated with government bonds. The total amount of compensation will be determined by a special committee, and the money will be paid by the newly established "Nationalized Industry Foundation," which will use the net profit of the industry to purchase bonds.

Soviet Occupation Authorities Prepare for Currency Reform in East Germany; Berlin Allied Control Council Shows Signs of Disintegration 46

[Reuters Berlin, 11th] Germans close to the Soviet military government revealed that the Soviet military government in Germany is actively preparing to announce the implementation of currency reform in East Germany within hours after the West German currency reform recommended in the London Six-Nation Conference communiqué is realized. Political figures believe that the recent disputes over passenger travel between West Germany and the Soviet occupation zone are a prelude to the implementation of East German currency reform. At the beginning of the implementation, traffic between the east and west occupation zones may be closed for several days. Sensitive Berliners, sensitive to the future of the Mark, are rushing to buy everything they can, even porcelain dictionaries, etc., in order to retain their value.

[Associated Press Berlin, 12th] West German currency reform seems imminent, with the aim of recovering 70 to 90 percent of the existing currency. Although officials refused to comment, non-official sources said that the full picture of the plan of the United States, Britain, and France is to make West Germany stand on an economically self-sufficient basis. (1) The West German New Mark does not immediately have value in the international market, and its area of use is limited, but it is hoped that it will eventually have the international value of the American dollar triangle. (2) This currency reform will be the most severe action in Western Europe. (3) The new currency is backed by West Germany's productivity, and the amount of its issuance is limited to the amount of production.

[Associated Press Berlin, 11th] A Soviet official newspaper hinted on the 11th that the Soviet Union intends to withdraw from the Four-Power Control Berlin Committee and control the city on its own. Some members of the Allied Control Council have stopped or abandoned their work due to the Soviet Union's withdrawal, and the whole council is showing signs of disintegration. According to today's editorial in a Soviet-controlled newspaper, the Soviet authorities are now weighing the pros and cons of two options: continuing to jointly administer the city by the four countries, or directly negotiating with the German authorities by the Soviet occupation government. If the latter path is taken, then Berlin is in the Soviet occupation zone, and the Soviet regime's assembly in Berlin is beyond dispute.

[Associated Press Berlin, 11th] The Brandenburg provincial government in the Soviet occupation zone of Germany today prohibited residents from moving to the British and American occupation zones. This kind of ban is still the first time.

Railway Freight Transport Between Berlin and West German Occupation Zone Has Resumed; Food and Fuel Urgently Needed for Two Million Residents 47

[Associated Press Berlin, 12th] British military authorities announced today that Britain and the Soviet Union have reached an agreement on restoring railway freight transport between West Germany and Berlin.

[United Press Berlin, 12th] US transportation officials said on the 12th that the Soviet Union had intentionally allowed 27 trains from West Germany to Berlin to pass through the Helmstedt iron rail barrier crossing the Soviet area.

[United Press Berlin, 12th] The Soviet Army cut off freight cars from West Germany to Berlin on the 12th, "pending further notice," creating a crisis in the supply of food and coal to Berlin's two million residents. U.S. Army Commander General Clay condemned the Soviet action and denied the Soviet excuse of Berlin traffic congestion. Clay also said that the food supply here is "limited" and that he may not take action temporarily in order to gather information. U.S. troops stationed at the border said that on the 12th, German and Allied cargo troops were blocked from passing through the Soviet occupation zone.

U.S. Representative Urges Security Council Approval of Atomic Energy Control Plan; Soviet Union Expected to Use Veto 48

[United Press International, Lake Success, 11th] The United Nations Security Council's vote on the U.S. atomic energy control plan has been postponed until next week. The Soviet Union is expected to use its veto power. For two years, the Soviet Union has vigorously contended within the Atomic Energy Commission. However, the commission does not have veto power. Three weeks ago, the commission voted in favor of the plan despite Soviet opposition, and the plan was submitted to the Security Council for discussion.

U.S. Deputy Representative Jessup today moved that the Security Council approve the U.S. plan. Soviet Deputy Foreign Minister Gromyko requested to speak at the Wednesday meeting next week to prevent its immediate vote. According to Jessup, the governments of all nations face only two paths: to continue the atomic arms race or to agree to an international control plan that all nations can trust. All nine members of the Security Council, except for the Soviet Union and Ukraine, support Jessup's resolution. British Representative Jebb pointed out that scientific inventions have made people believe that absolute sovereignty cannot exist for the sake of maintaining civilization. The basic question is whether countries should accept the supervision of a supranational authority in the area of atomic energy. Otherwise, under the arms race, civilization will eventually be destroyed. The Soviet Union, however, demands that the United States first dismantle its atomic bombs and then implement controls.

U.S. House Passes Refugee Admission Bill 49

[United Press International, Washington, 11th] The U.S. House of Representatives today passed a bill by a vote of 289 to 91, allowing 202,000 displaced Europeans and an unspecified number of orphans to enter the country. The restrictions are far fewer than those in the bill passed by the Senate. A joint committee of the two houses is now seeking a compromise.

[Our Newspaper Report] New York, 12th Broadcast: According to the U.S. State Department, the U.S. has received a request to send three aircraft and three cruisers to assist in monitoring the implementation of the Arab-Israeli truce.

Seven U.S. military officers and one Swedish military officer have arrived in Haifa to supervise the ceasefire. The remaining personnel have been dispatched to the Jordanian capital.

[Reuters, London, 12th] It is expected that the truce observers under the command of United Nations Palestine Mediator Bernadotte will be stationed on the various battle lines in the Holy Land from the 12th to prevent any further violations of the ceasefire order. Bernadotte issued a public statement in Cairo yesterday, listing four instances of alleged Jewish violations of the ceasefire order, and then cabled the Security Council requesting the urgent allocation of aircraft and coastal patrol boats for monitoring the ceasefire.

Arab League Secretary-General Azzam has solemnly declared to Bernadotte that if the Jewish side provokes first, the Arab forces will retaliate. The Israeli military commander has also stated that if the Jewish forces are attacked by the Arab forces, the Jewish forces will not hesitate to retaliate immediately.

Tel Aviv-Jerusalem Highway Reopened 51

In addition to the mutual accusations of violations of the ceasefire order, a major development in the Holy Land yesterday was the reopening of the Tel Aviv-Jerusalem highway, which had been closed since the outbreak of the war. The Jewish side has stated that they have opened a new route next to the Arab Legion blockade station at El-Uut Al-Ara, and supplies are being continuously supplied to the 100,000 Jews in the new urban area of Jerusalem through this new route.

Both Sides Accuse Each Other of Violating Ceasefire Order 52

A Jewish spokesperson stated that for twelve hours after the ceasefire order came into effect at 10:00 a.m. local time, fierce fighting continued in the area south of Lake Tiberias and in the Jordan River basin. Syrian forces, under the cover of armored vehicles, artillery, and aircraft, continued their attacks in the vicinity of Ha-Yarden and Ya'akov until yesterday evening. The Arab side's accusations include: (1) Ninety minutes after the ceasefire order came into effect, Jewish artillerymen in the Shuk Ya'ala district of Jerusalem killed several Jordanian soldiers; (2) Forty minutes after the ceasefire order came into effect, Jewish soldiers near the Hadassah Hospital on Mount Scopus in Jerusalem fired on Arab civilians; (3) Several hours after the ceasefire order came into effect, a Jewish aircraft dropped several bombs on Damascus, the capital of Syria; (4) On the border between Syria and Palestine, Jewish forces failed to cease firing on time.

Nishio's Accusations Expected to Affect the Entire Situation

Three Reasons for the Rice Price Surge; Mayor Reports on Handling Measures; Urgently Cables Central Government to Transport 300,000 Shi of Grain to Aid Shanghai 62

[Our Newspaper Report] The price of rice in the city has been soaring unprecedentedly for days, with no end in sight. In the Fengjing area, there have been incidents of rice looting, affecting the transport of rice to Shanghai from the area, causing public anxiety. This is a matter of great importance to people's livelihoods. Mayor Wu specially invited reporters to the municipal government conference room at 5:00 p.m. yesterday to report on the countermeasures that the municipal authorities are currently striving to implement. Mayor Wu believes that there are three causes for the rice price surge: (1) the period between harvests, (2) large-scale smuggling of rice to Jiangbei, and (3) the impact of the implementation of the foreign exchange certificate method. The authorities are currently dealing with the situation in two ways: (1) Regarding the rice looting in the Jingyi area, a telegram has been sent to the Jiangsu Provincial Government requesting its immediate suppression and asking it to provide better protection for rice merchants transporting rice in the future. (2) A telegram has been urgently sent to Premier Weng Wenhao of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Food Guan Jiyu, urging them to rush the transportation of 300,000 shi of rice allocated from distant production areas to Shanghai by the end of the month to supply the people's food.

It is confirmed that Mayor Wu, feeling deeply frustrated by the recent inability to curb the soaring prices in the city, formally tendered his resignation to Premier Weng Wenhao of the Executive Yuan on the 9th of this month. When asked about this at yesterday's press conference, Wu confirmed it. However, because Premier Weng strongly urged him to stay and promised to seek a good solution, his intention to resign has been abandoned, and he has decided to reluctantly continue for the time being.

1,400 Tons of American Rice to Arrive the Day After Tomorrow 63

The first batch of 12,000 tons of rice under American aid, purchased by the American side in Siam and transported by our China Merchants Steam Navigation Company ships, has already set sail from Bangkok and is now en route to China. Mayor Wu Criticizes Jiaotong University's Open Letter; Questions the Anti-Support Japan Event; Investigating Whether There Are Manipulators 64

[Our Newspaper Report] Mayor Wu, at yesterday afternoon's press conference, again criticized the Jiaotong University students' initiation of the "Oppose the United States Supporting Japan" march, and believed that the "Open Letter to Mayor Wu" from the Jiaotong University Student Union yesterday was deliberately confusing public opinion and had simply forgotten that they were Chinese. The reason why the municipal government raised questions to the school was to investigate whether this anti-American movement was being manipulated. If it was purely a patriotic student movement, the municipal government would definitely sympathize and assist. If it was instigated by the Communists, it would be strictly investigated. The various facts presented are sufficient to prove that this march was a planned conspiracy: On June 3rd, the student union held a symposium to oppose the United States supporting Japan. Except for Mayor Wu, all those invited were leftist professors, creating a one-sided situation, with the purpose of building momentum. The day after the symposium, a representative meeting of various departments was immediately held to vote to take unified action, and it was decided that more than a hundred organizations would carry out a march on the 5th. After summarizing the events, three points can be proven: (1) The so-called anti-American support Japan march was obviously decided before the representative meeting of various departments was held. (2) A small number of Jiaotong University students colluded and contacted the initiators of the conspiracy beforehand, without reporting to the majority of students. (3) The representative meeting of various departments was controlled and manipulated by thirty or so absolutely minority students.

Mayor's Agitated Attitude

Mayor Wu's attitude was quite agitated yesterday. He said that the crux of the problem was whether there was manipulation behind the march. The various questions raised by the municipal government were based on the above principles. If the school could answer each question clearly and prove that it was a purely patriotic student movement, then Wu would personally apologize to Jiaotong University.

As for the tenth point raised in the student union's open letter (original text: In your first so-called seven "inquiries," you asked six "who's," and in the so-called eight "re-inquiries," you asked nine "who's." May we ask, in today's era of secret arrests and the endless "automatic" disappearances, what intentions do you have in pursuing "who's"?), Mayor Wu's reply was: The purpose is to make the conspiratorial actions of the conspirators public to society, hoping to subject them to moral and legal sanctions. If the students' anti-American support Japan is purely a patriotic action, then the organizers should be able to stand up and speak out. Only spies would shirk responsibility from each other.

Guarantee of Public Interrogation Mayor Wu also absolutely guaranteed that the municipal government's investigation of the initiating students would be completely open. In the future, when the police department summons them, the press will also be invited to attend and the content will be made public, allowing the citizens of the city to judge for themselves.

Mayor Wu finally revealed the three stages of the Communist Party as (1) a small number of people hijack the public, (2) an organized minority uses an unorganized majority, (3) using appealing names to disrupt public order.

Municipal Meeting Passes Supplementary Measures for Grain Merchant Registration 65

[Our Newspaper Report] The Shanghai Municipal Supplementary Measures for the Provisional Grain Merchant Registration has been approved by the municipal meeting. Grain merchant registration will begin after the municipal government issues an order. The measures have a total of nine articles. Excerpts are selected below: Article 2, All grain merchants applying for registration shall follow the following regulations: (1) Those who have been open for more than two years before the end of February of the 37th year (1948) and have never ceased operations shall submit supporting documents or account books for review. (2) Those who have been open for less than two years before the end of February of the 37th year (1948), in addition to complying with the provisions of the preceding paragraph, shall also provide written certification from two grain merchants holding business licenses, in accordance with the principles for preventing merchants from speculating and profiteering, confirming that they are legitimate merchants and have no speculative or profiteering behavior, before being reviewed. (3) Those who have opened after March 1 of the 37th year (1948), in addition to submitting supporting documents in accordance with the provisions of the preceding paragraph, must also be inspected on-site by personnel dispatched by the Social Bureau before being reviewed and approved. Article 3, Even if the conditions of the preceding paragraphs are met, the application shall still be rejected if any of the following circumstances are found: (1) Having violated the Grain Management Regulations during Extraordinary Periods and having been penalized on record. (2) Having been subject to penalties greater than a warning for failing to comply with regulations when selling government-sold rice or household rice. Article 4, The capital stipulated in Article 2 of the Grain Merchant Registration Rules shall be proven in accordance with the following methods: (1) For company organizations, a copy of the company license shall be sent. (2) For partnerships, a certificate of capital collected by the firm or a copy of the partnership agreement and relevant account books shall be provided. (3) For sole proprietorships, capital account books and bank deposit certificates shall be provided. (4) The same applies to those applying to change registration due to increased capital. Article 7, Those who have not registered but have joined the relevant guild before the implementation of these measures shall complete registration within one month after the implementation of these measures. If the registration does not meet the standards, the guild shall revoke their membership, the same as those who do not apply for registration.

Unprecedented Oil Shortage; Does It Only Affect Traffic Order? Why Does the Authorities Ignore It? 69

[Our Newspaper Report] The oil shortage in this city not only has not improved due to price adjustments, but on the contrary, has become more serious in recent days. The congestion at each gas station is almost out of control. Every day, around 10:00 a.m., the supply is sold out, resulting in scrambling and traffic jams, which are often heard of.

There are currently 52 gas stations in Shanghai, but the gasoline supply for each station in May and June has decreased by 25% daily, meaning that the daily allocation for each station is only 300 to 900 gallons. Moreover, a small number of unscrupulous gas stations are taking the opportunity to channel oil into the black market, resulting in black market oil prices exceeding the legal price by more than double per gallon. This situation has become an open secret, but the relevant authorities are ignoring it and have not taken effective measures to stop it. In addition, each company routinely stops supplying oil on holidays, which further exacerbates the severity of the oil shortage.

Recently, there are often many vehicles that rush to the gas stations before dawn to wait, queuing up like a single long snake, but when it is about to be their turn to refuel, the gas station suddenly announces that it is sold out. Therefore, wasting time for four or five hours, and still not getting a drop of oil, has become commonplace.

Compensation Material Ship Unprecedentedly Searched Someone Secretly Reported Hai'e Smuggling Involving Senior Supervising Officer on Board 70

According to regulations, ships carrying Japanese compensation materials to China are exempt from inspection. Most of the first batch of Japanese compensation materials have been transported to Shanghai so far, and there are still thousands of tons of materials en route to China. Among them, 3,000 tons were transported to Shanghai by the "Hai'e" ship at 5:00 p.m. yesterday. The customs suddenly received a secret report claiming that in addition to Japanese compensation materials, the ship also carried a large amount of Japanese goods prepared for smuggling, and that this smuggled cargo was colluded by a senior officer on the ship supervising Japanese compensation materials and a major smuggling company in Shanghai in an attempt to smuggle in. Based on this secret report, the customs immediately secretly dispatched a number of officers to conduct an unprecedented search when the ship docked and unloaded. The search took a long time, and the customs may announce the situation of the seized smuggled goods today. After this smuggling incident, the customs will closely monitor ships carrying Japanese compensation materials in the future. The last ship carrying the first batch of Japanese compensation materials, the Zizhong (自忠), is now carrying 3,000 tons en route to Shanghai, which is expected to arrive in mid-June. It is possible that it also carries smuggled goods.

Four Defendants in French Ship Drug Case Released on Bail 71

In the case of the French mail ship Antelopes' crew members smuggling opium, four people including the foreman of the fueling room, A. The guarantor and the four bailed persons all stated that they were willing to comply, so bail was granted.

However, the Senate's proposal was not approved by the central government. The Ministry of Finance has again ordered the Municipal Finance Bureau to levy the business tax for this year according to the revised tax rate, starting from January 1st. As the Finance Bureau had previously invited people to levy the spring business tax according to the Senate's decision and had already started collecting it at the original tax rate, changing to the revised tax rate now would require businesses to pay an additional half or 20% for the spring tax collection (the new tax rate levies the tax rate on business income; increasing two percent on income), which would inevitably arouse resentment among businesses and increase the difficulty of collection. Yesterday, the bureau submitted the case to the Senate for reconsideration to decide on a course of action.

Social Affairs Bureau Sets Standards for Height and Weight of Young Workers 80

[Report from Our Newspaper] The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has recently received instructions from the Ministry of Social Affairs to establish standards for height and weight of young workers in the Southeast region of our country and hopes that factories will be instructed to comply. There is a section of explanation at the front, roughly saying: "Although the Factory Law has age restrictions on child labor, our country has not yet implemented a birth certificate system, which makes implementation very difficult. Now, after deliberation by the Committee for Determining the Height and Weight of Child Labor, the standard for young workers in the Southeast region is established, and all child laborers are renamed young workers." The standards for height and weight of young workers in the Southeast region are as follows: (1) The height of male young workers aged 14 in factories and mines should be at least 140 cm, and the weight should be 34.5 kg. The height of female young workers should be at least 142.5 cm, and the weight should be 35 kg. Young workers of both sexes who do not meet either standard will be prohibited from employment. (2) If male workers in factories and mines are 16 years old but their height is less than 161 cm and their weight is less than 50.5 kg, or if female workers' height is less than 155 cm and their weight is less than 47.5 kg, they will be regarded as young workers. (3) Within one year after the implementation of this standard, existing young workers in various factories who do not meet the standard for the age of 14 will not be eliminated for the time being, but they must be registered upon the start of implementation, and those who do not meet the standard after one year will be eliminated. However, new young workers must still be employed in accordance with this standard. (4) This standard will be implemented from July 1st, and is temporarily limited to Jiangsu Province and the two cities of Nanjing and Shanghai.

Extremely Hot Yesterday, Maximum Temperature of 102 Degrees, Another Low-Pressure System May Turn into a Typhoon 97

[Report from Our Newspaper] The weather was extremely hot yesterday. The minimum temperature was 74.7 degrees Fahrenheit, and the maximum temperature in the afternoon reached 102 degrees Fahrenheit, which is not much different from the highest temperature in Shanghai in June of the 23rd year of the Republic, which was 102.8 degrees Fahrenheit. It has also exceeded the highest temperature in June of last year. Regarding the report that a typhoon occurred in the sea off Hong Kong, according to the Shanghai Meteorological Observatory, this is only a summer low-pressure system on the mainland, which has been lingering in Hong Kong for about three days and is not a typhoon. Typhoons move very quickly. However, there is another low-pressure system that may turn into a typhoon, but it has no impact on the ports in eastern China. It is located at 133 degrees east longitude and 27.5 degrees north latitude, south of Kyushu, Japan, and is currently moving north. Its wind speed is 60 knots per hour. Ships traveling to and from Japanese ports from Shanghai should pay attention.

Decided That Rent Should Be Paid First Before Return of Occupied Civilian Land, Review Council Extends Conclusion Due to Unfinished Business 104

The Review Council for the Use of Enemy and Puppet Occupied Civilian Land in Shanghai by Central Government Agencies of the Executive Yuan held its fourth meeting at the Municipal Government Conference Room at 3 PM yesterday. Those present included Wu Guozhen, who also served as the Chairman, Zhu Ping, Xiang Changquan, Xie Haoling, Ma Shaoji, Shen Naizheng, Xu Xiajun, and more than thirty others. The meeting was chaired by Chairman Wu Guozhen. The council first approved the opinions of the review committees in each subcommittee on a case-by-case basis, and then resolved to recommend that the Executive Yuan pay rent in advance for the use of enemy and puppet occupied civilian land in Shanghai by various central government agencies, before completing the procedures for requisition or actually returning the land to its owners. The methods are as follows: (1) The rent shall be paid at the standard of the general rent in the local area. (2) If the relevant user agency does not have a budget for the rent to be paid, it should immediately request the Executive Yuan to add and allocate funds, and the council will recommend that the Executive Yuan approve it. (3) The rent shall be paid from the date on which the relevant user agency received and used the land.

The council had originally decided to conclude its work at yesterday's fourth meeting, but since the actual business could not be completed, some members requested an extension. The council approved this request and decided to extend the conclusion date until the actual business is completed.

Increasing Work Efficiency by Utilizing Both Hands Simultaneously 105

[Special Report from Our Newspaper] The twentieth century is an era of intense competition where the superior prevail and the inferior are eliminated. Efficiency is crucial in all work, especially in countries with highly developed industries. Their scientists and entrepreneurs are constantly researching: How can work efficiency be increased? How can time and manpower be saved? How can waste be reduced and wealth increased?

Yesterday, the Shanghai branch of the Chinese Industrial Management Association was established. As part of the entertainment program, a newly borrowed American film on "motion study" was shown. This film represents research on the efficiency of manual labor, the result of the painstaking efforts of experts at the University of Iowa in the United States. They discovered that in ordinary daily manual tasks, people unknowingly waste a significant amount of time and energy due to ignorance and neglect, time and energy that could be saved.

Short Process, Ten Steps: The film first demonstrated that any manual task can be divided into several steps of motion. For example, taking a pen from a pen holder, signing a document, and then returning the pen to the holder can be broken down as follows: Reaching for the pen holder is the first step. Selecting a specific pen from the holder is the second step. Gripping the pen is the third step. Bringing the pen closer to oneself is the fourth step. Pointing the pen tip to the area on the paper where the signature should be placed is the fifth step. Starting to sign is the sixth step. After signing, returning the pen to the pen holder is the seventh step. Locating the pen's position in the holder is the eighth step. Inserting the pen into the holder is the ninth step. Retracting the hand is the tenth step. This short process can be analyzed into as many as ten movements, some involving the shoulder muscles, others involving the elbow muscles, and still others involving the wrist muscles. The movements of the shoulder and elbow require more effort and take more time. After analyzing these movements, the scientists found that in most tasks, many shoulder and elbow movements can be reduced or replaced.

The Left Hand is Often Useless: The film also showed that in ordinary manual tasks, the left hand is often nearly useless. For example, when inserting thirty plugs into thirty holes on a wooden board, most people would hold a large handful of plugs in their left hand and then use their right hand to pick them out one by one and insert them. Although both hands are moving, only one hand can be said to be effectively working, which greatly reduces work efficiency.

Based on the above analysis, a method was developed to increase the efficiency of both hands: that is, to minimize the movements of the shoulder and elbow as much as possible. When these movements cannot be reduced, the left and right hands should be used simultaneously in opposite and symmetrical directions.

The film continued to show a comparison of efficiency between the old method and the improved method. Using the aforementioned plug-insertion example, the improved movement involves both hands simultaneously reaching for the tray containing the plugs, each taking one plug. The elbows are then bent inward in opposite directions, and each hand inserts a plug into the wooden board. This symmetrical movement is continued, proving that the time spent can be greatly reduced.

Twenty Glasses of Ice Water Prepared Simultaneously: The work efficiency of a waiter in a coffee shop preparing ice water is an application of the above method. If a waiter needs to prepare twenty glasses of ice water, he might first put ice cubes one by one into each glass and then pour water into each glass. His hand moves back and forth, his movements are too monotonous, repetitive, and time-consuming. The improved method involves first creating a large wooden tray, the tray's bottom having a thickness equal to that of an ice cube, with twenty circular holes the size of the glass openings, precisely aligned with the twenty glasses. First, a thin board covers the glasses, and the wooden tray is placed on top of the board. A large amount of ice cubes is poured into the tray and spread evenly by hand. Each of the twenty circular holes then contains an ice cube. The thin board is removed, and the twenty ice cubes fall into the twenty glasses simultaneously. Then, two rubber tubes are connected to the water source, and each hand holds one tube, pouring water simultaneously. In no time, twenty glasses of ice water are prepared simultaneously.

Unknowingly Adding So Much Wealth: Banks must send account statements to customers at the end of each month. Employees use their left hand to hold an envelope and their right hand to take an account statement, placing hundreds or thousands of statements into envelopes one by one, wasting so much time in the process. If the envelopes are divided into two piles and placed on the table, with the openings facing outwards and the middles held down lightly with an object, both hands can simultaneously take one statement each and insert them into the envelopes on either side. The work can be completed in less than half the time.

Similar examples of increasing efficiency by using both hands simultaneously and reducing unnecessary movements can be studied and implemented at any time in factories, offices, candy stores, and other workplaces that require manual labor. The film presented many comparisons, ending with the sound of a "tick-tock" clock. It tells us: If humans can make good use of every "tick-tock," they can unknowingly create so much more wealth!

The Chinese Industrial Management Association Shanghai Branch Established: Screening of Motion Study Film Newly Borrowed from America

National Bank Regulations on the Sale of Foreign Exchange Settlement Certificates Between Shanghai and Other Ports 106

[Report from Our Newspaper] Regarding the trading of foreign exchange settlement certificates between Shanghai and other ports, the Central Bank recently notified all designated banks with letter No. 141 to handle matters according to the following procedures.

(1) Foreign exchange settlement certificates from other ports may be sold in Shanghai, and foreign exchange settlement certificates required by other ports may also be purchased from Shanghai.

(2) If a designated bank in another port needs to sell foreign exchange settlement certificates, it may telegraph the amount it intends to sell to its Shanghai branch office so that the branch can be responsible for settling the sale with the Central Bank's Business Bureau in the future.

(3) The Shanghai branch office of the designated bank may, based on the above telegram, apply to the Central Bank for a special foreign exchange settlement certificate valid for seven days, to facilitate its sale in Shanghai.

(4) Once the original foreign exchange settlement certificate is sent from the designated bank in another port, it should be immediately submitted to the Central Bank's Business Bureau for cancellation.

(5) After the designated bank in Shanghai purchases foreign exchange settlement certificates on behalf of its branch office in another port, it may submit them to the Central Bank's Business Bureau. Upon submission, the Business Bureau may telegraph the Central Bank's branch in the other port, in order that the branch in the other port can issue special foreign exchange settlement certificates to the designated bank's branch office in that port.

(6) The above procedures are temporarily limited to transactions between Shanghai and other ports. Transactions between other ports are not applicable. The market for trading foreign exchange settlement certificates was very stable yesterday. 540,000 were traded, with HSBC selling the most. The high price of 620,000 from the day before was the result of a direct transaction between buyers and sellers and did not go through a designated bank. A large company sold more than 4,300 US dollars at this high price.

Shortage of Arrivals, Rising Production Costs: Rice Prices Soar, Special High-Quality Japonica Rice Approaches the 10 Million Yuan Mark 107

[Report from Our Newspaper] After the Dragon Boat Festival, rice prices soared wildly, threatening to approach the ten million mark. Yesterday, special high-quality Japonica rice in the North City market reached a new high of 9.3 million yuan per shi (unit of dry measure). Door-to-door rice shops, after adding a 6% legal profit and transportation costs, reached approximately 9.78 million yuan. Breaking the ten million mark is not far off.

According to relevant sources, the reasons for the recent surge in rice prices are: (1) hoarders are speculating and unwilling to sell; (2) arrivals have been scarce in the past two days, totaling only slightly over 4,000 shi; (3) yesterday morning, a rice boat from Fengjing, carrying 160 shi of rice, was robbed by impoverished people; (4) the wild rise in prices of all goods is stimulating rice prices; (5) rice prices in producing areas are also rising, with Wuxi, Songjiang, and other places reaching 8.5 million yuan per shi.

Flour: Bidding did not commence because economic police were strictly monitoring transactions at the market and inspecting permits. With the prices of all goods rising, the market was strong, but people were afraid of interference from the economic police, so no one dared to call out prices. The bidding session ended without any transactions. In the after-market, old truck and military ship flour were bid at 2.8 million, and large bran at 2.6 million, each rising by about 100,000. The China Trust Bureau continued to release flour at unchanged prices. New wheat was traded at 3.9 million, and old wheat at 4 million.

Grains: Continued to be firm. People remained exceptionally bullish due to the unabated rise in prices of various goods, and sellers were unwilling to sell much. Soybean prices were reported to have risen by 150,000 yuan due to high costs. High-quality Hanzhou miscellaneous beans were priced at 4.8 million. Millet and red sorghum continued to rise by 200,000 yuan under the continued purchases from the northern gangs. Mung beans were being absorbed by the southern Chinese gangs, rising by 3-400,000. New broad beans had fewer customers and abundant arrivals, uniquely falling by 300,000. The price of naked barley also changed little. Sesame increased by 3-400,000. Raw peanuts were traded very little, with raw peanuts from Dawenkou traded at 17.8 million.

Cooking Oil: The upward trend continued. People were still bullish, and with easy money and abundant credit, buying was still strong. Most sellers were holding their goods and not selling. Soybean oil opened at 20.08 million, then Dalian soybean oil at 21.1 million, an increase of 1 million. Rapeseed oil rose by 800,000, to 19.8 million. Raw oil and sesame oil from small trucks each rose by 1 million, and soybean cake rose by 12-30,000.

Concerned Parties Analyze Reasons for Loose Monetary Policy 108

[Report from Our Newspaper] The June price surge is still in full swing. Although the authorities have been selling materials and tightening credit, there has been no effect so far. According to observations by relevant parties, the main reason for this price surge is the extremely loose monetary policy. The excessive amount of capital in the market is due to the following factors: (1) More than half of the silkworm cocoon loans issued in the spring have now flowed into urban areas, estimated to be over 4 trillion yuan; (2) Due to the overall situation, funds from North China are still flowing south continuously, averaging over 1 trillion yuan per day, mostly in cash, causing frequent receipts and payments in Shanghai's banks and firms; (3) The release of funds by the National Bank, for the Dragon Boat Festival alone, is estimated to be around 1 trillion yuan. (4) Since the ban on post-dated checks, the number of circulating promissory notes has greatly increased. With their function equivalent to large banknotes, the expansion of credit naturally affects prices. The current authorities' hope rests on the US aid materials that are about to arrive. When the materials are sold and distributed in tandem, prices may be temporarily stabilized.

Yesterday, the monetary policy in Shanghai was still extremely loose. The market interest rate was between 0.24 and 0.25. The four banks, two bureaus, and one treasury had a net deficit of 550 billion in the clearing of checks and notes. Among them, the Central Bank had a deficit of 64 billion, the Bank of China 419.1 billion, the Bank of Communications 106.9 billion, the Farmers Bank 11.4 billion, the China Trust Bureau 10.1 billion, the Postal Remittances Bureau 50.1 billion, and the Central Cooperative Treasury 11.4 billion. Commercial banks and firms had a net deficit of 247.8 billion in the large exchange and a net surplus of 551 billion in the small exchange. Foreign banks in Shanghai had a total net surplus of 248.8 billion.

Customers Enthusiastically Bullish and Compete to Buy: Cotton Yarn Prices Rise Again, Textile Traders Sell Short, Market Still Rising 109

Yesterday, the cotton yarn market was characterized by loose monetary policy. Although the China Textile Corporation (CTC) was still distributing a large amount of yarn, the market sentiment was unanimously bullish, and people were scrambling to buy. Outside buyers were particularly eager. 42-count Blue Phoenix fine yarn opened high at 30 million yuan. Subsequently, due to competition from Tianjin and Guangdong gangs, the market climbed again, closing at 48.5 million yuan, a sharp increase of 5.5 million yuan compared to before the holiday. The remaining 40, 32, 20, 16-count and other coarse and fine yarns uniformly rose by 1.3-4 million and over 10%, respectively.

Yesterday, the cotton cloth market had abundant idle funds flowing into Shanghai, and buying interest was exceptionally strong. 12-pound Dragon Head fine cloth jumped 200,000 yuan at the opening. Subsequently, due to the industry's ample capital and vigorous purchases, coupled with large purchases by the Tianjin gang, the market gradually rose to 9.59 million yuan. Around 10 o'clock, when CTC announced the sale of Dragon Head cloth with posted prices, market sentiment calmed down, and there was a lot of short-selling by traders. Customer interest turned dull, finally closing at 9.55 million yuan, continuing to rise by 350,000 yuan compared to the previous day. In addition, Four Gentlemen flannel was eagerly absorbed by the Hankou gang, and spot prices rose by 340,000 yuan. The prices of other cloths also rose strongly.

Guangdong Merchants Raise Five Opinions After Implementation of New Foreign Exchange Settlement Measures 118

[Report from Our Newspaper] Guangzhou import and export merchants recently submitted five opinions to the Central Bank regarding the implementation of the new foreign exchange settlement measures, requesting a reply: (1) To avoid manipulation by large players, foreign exchange settlement certificates should be used in separate zones, with the administrative regions of the local export management associations serving as the standard for zoning; (2) To encourage exports and provide an outlet for surplus foreign exchange settlement certificates, the government is requested to increase import quotas, relax the registration qualifications for importers, and the Central Bank is requested to purchase certificates at market prices; (3) In accordance with Articles 18 and 20 of the new measures, a public market should be established to determine the market price of foreign exchange settlement certificates; and foreign exchange settlement certificate current accounts should be opened so that merchants can buy and sell independently and not be subject to monopoly manipulation by large players; (4) Customs' valuation of import and export commodities should be based on facts, with exports based on local market prices and imports based on merchants' purchase prices; (5) The issuance of special foreign exchange settlement certificates should be made public and restricted. The Central Bank and the Export Management Committee will respond to the above five opinions in the coming days.

The Anglo-Chinese Incident: A Preliminary Resolution Reached 126

Jinzhong Issues a Letter Clarifying the Sequence of Events

[Our Paper's Report] The conflict between students from Jinhua Anglo-Chinese University and Jinzhong High School has been preliminarily resolved following mediation by officials dispatched by the Ministry of Education in conjunction with the Director of the Zhejiang Education Bureau. However, Jinzhong High School believes that Anglo-Chinese University's account is inconsistent with the facts. They recently sent a letter to this newspaper stating, in brief: The incident occurred on the evening of May 28th. At that time, our school students were holding a variety show to bid farewell to graduating students. Due to the limited space, guests were generally declined. Several dozen Anglo-Chinese University students forcibly tried to enter, and after repeated dissuasion by our school students and the Director of Moral Education proved ineffective, Headmaster Hu repeatedly explained and apologized, but it was still ineffective. As a last resort, they were allowed to enter. At the time, order in the venue was normal, and there was absolutely no booing. As the first act had just ended, an Anglo-Chinese University student suddenly went on stage and shouted that since Jinzhong High School was not entertaining guests, Anglo-Chinese University students should all leave together. After retreating to the gate, they gathered in increasing numbers, their momentum growing menacing, which then triggered the conflict. When Anglo-Chinese University's Dean of Academic Affairs Cai and others came to the school, they were also unable to stop the students' riot. Later, County Magistrate Yang arrived, but the Anglo-Chinese University students continued to besiege him, trapping him in our school for several hours. The next morning, Commander Chen of the 102nd Brigade of the Army came to the school and genuinely intended to mediate. Headmaster Hu told him that the Anglo-Chinese University students must first stop the attack before negotiating, and there was no truth to the claim that he avoided meeting with them.

Furthermore, Jinzhong's Shanghai alumni have also published a "Letter to People from All Walks of Life," stating in brief: "Our alma mater's variety show was purely an internal school activity, not a public performance. Anglo-Chinese University students had no right to interfere. Furthermore, Headmaster Hu had already explained politely and even made concessions by allowing them to enter. How could they have engaged in such violent behavior?" They also put forward five demands: (1) Replace the president of Anglo-Chinese University; (2) Severely punish the perpetrators; (3) Compensate for all losses of books, instruments, school buildings, and school equipment, as well as medical expenses; (4) Publicly apologize; (5) Guarantee that similar incidents will not occur in the future.

U.S. Congress Passes the Smith-Mundt Act, to Exchange Academic and Technical Personnel 136

[Our Paper's Nanjing, 12th Dispatch] In order to improve other countries' correct understanding of the United States and the mutual understanding of their peoples, the U.S. government, through Congress, passed the "United States Information and Educational Exchange Act of 1948," also known as the "Smith-Mundt Act." The main points of the act are as follows: (1) Purpose: To enable other countries to have a correct understanding of the United States and to promote mutual understanding between the peoples of both sides, the following steps will be taken: (a) Providing news: The President, Secretary of State, and government agencies related to foreign affairs shall communicate matters related to the U.S. government and people, and policies declared by Congress, to other countries. (b) Educational exchange: The programs include the exchange of academic and technical personnel, the exchange of technical and other services, and the development and exchange of education, science, and art. (2) Exchange of personnel and technology: The Secretary of State may establish exchange personnel programs on a reciprocal basis; such personnel include students, technical trainees, teachers, lecturers, professors, and various experts; and may use existing well-known private institutions to promote the realization of the above tasks. The Secretary of State may assist schools, libraries, and other social undertakings established by people in other countries, but shall not interfere with the policies of these private institutions or violate democratic beliefs. (3) Not sending experts: If a foreign government needs a certain technical expert and the United States is willing to cooperate, the Secretary of State may appoint personnel from U.S. government agencies to serve, subject to the agency's consent. First, the Secretary of State must confirm that it is beneficial to the United States; second, the foreign government must provide remuneration and salaries; and third, military technical personnel are not included. (4) Requisition of government agencies: The Secretary of State may requisition the materials and personnel of other government agencies to meet the requests of foreign governments. In order to implement this policy, each agency should be encouraged as much as possible to entrust suitable private institutions to complete the implementation. (5) Overseas propaganda: The propaganda policy should focus on maximizing the use of private or private institutions. If suitable private propaganda institutions exist, government propaganda agencies must be reduced and withdrawn. Second, the government does not control shortwave broadcasting or have exclusive government propaganda tools. (6) Advisory Committee: Two advisory committees on information and educational exchange shall be established under this act. Each committee shall have five members, appointed by the President, but government officials may not serve. The advisory members are remunerated for their positions. The tasks of the two committees are to conduct research, issue warnings, and provide policy recommendations. (7) Expenses: The Secretary of State has the right to transfer funds to other agencies in need. (8) Management procedures: The State Department shall allocate funds and materials to the government or private agencies entrusted. It shall supply, sell, and lease news materials and tools, and at the same time, it shall make the most of government assets and tools. (9) External funds: The State Department may accept or request funds from any domestic or foreign public or private institution for public benefit. (10) Others: To implement this act, the State Department should cooperate with private institutions as much as possible, such as newspapers, magazines, radio stations, and film companies, and enter into contracts or other methods with them to ensure that all private institutions and groups from different industries participate in the cooperation to realize the purpose of this act as much as possible.

[British Information Services, London Dispatch] British female basketball players have expressed dissatisfaction with the fact that the women's events in the World Games are limited to swimming, track and field, and a few other events. They believe that the International Olympic Committee should include women's basketball and volleyball events, as these two competitions are most suitable for women and are also very popular in the Americas and the Caribbean.

Scientific Arrangement of the World Games Venue

British scientists, surveyors, electrical, radio, and telegraph engineers are currently busy working for the upcoming Olympic World Games to be held in London. Britain plans to equip the World Games venue with the latest equipment. British scientists are conducting various experiments, such as electrical timing, precision measuring instruments, telephone lines, radio control for races, electrical judging machines, signaling devices, and gas flames illuminating the entire venue, striving for perfection.

New Zealand Athletes Arrive in Britain

The New Zealand team participating in the World Games arrived here at the end of last month, so the team can still train in Britain for nine weeks before the opening of the Games. It is reported that the travel expenses for the team from New Zealand to Britain are approximately 500 pounds per person.

Issue of World Games Commemorative Stamps 149

[British Information Services, London Dispatch] Britain has always regarded the issuance of stamps as a major industry, and special stamps are especially rare. Therefore, the commemorative stamps to be issued next month to celebrate the 14th World Games will be cherished by stamp collectors and athletes everywhere. The issuance of World Games commemorative stamps has been a long-standing tradition. The new stamps for 1948 will be divided into two and a half pence (ordinary stamps within the Empire), three pence, six pence, and one shilling and four pence. The two highest denominations are suitable for sending overseas airmail. However, these stamps will not be issued until the opening of the Games.

Reader's Opinion: Lack of Streetlights Leads to Bandit Activity 154

Residents of the Shuidaidian Road and North Baoxing Road Area Write to Appeal

Dear Editor: We live in the Shuidaidian Road area. Because it is remote, thieves are often active at night. Since last year, the streetlights there have not been lit at all. Even the electric lights that we paid to install are like ghost fires, making people feel terrified. Moreover, the company arbitrarily suspends power, so having lights is the same as not having lights. Recently, robberies have occurred frequently in the Shuidaidian Road and North Baoxing Road area. Even a kitchen knife can be used to rob homes. People living in the city cannot imagine that Shanghai has such a terrifying area. The police station recently published in major newspapers that if there are problems with the electric lights in the alleys, it can be reported to the bureau for processing, and power outages should not be used to deal with them, as this affects social security. Your newspaper is the voice of the people. We hope that you will publish this to bring it to the attention of the authorities, and we hope that the company will not privately suspend power anymore. The citizens will be very grateful!

Respectfully, Readers Li Shufu and Liu Dezhong
